KERAJAAN PERPADUAN: KESTABILAN DAN REFORMASI DALAM LANDASAN POLITIK BAHARU 1.	Kerajaan Perpaduan pimpinan Perdana Menteri, YAB Datoâ€™ Seri Anwar Ibrahim terus menunjukkan ketahanan melalui pendekatan kolaboratif antara komponen PH, BN, dan GPS. Berbanding naratif â€œkrisis politikâ€ yang didakwa sesetengah pihak, realiti semasa membuktikan bahawa kerajaan sekarang kekal utuh dengan sokongan majoriti yang kukuh dalam parlimen.  2.	Dalam sistem demokrasi berparlimen seperti Malaysia, kerajaan gabungan merupakan satu mekanisme biasa untuk memastikan kestabilan politik. Peletakan jawatan Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad sebenarnya mencerminkan proses demokrasi dalaman parti (PKR), bukannya petanda keruntuhan kerajaan. 3.	Geseran dalaman dalam sesebuah kerajaan gabungan adalah sesuatu yang normal. YAB Datoâ€™ Seri Anwar Ibrahim telah menunjukkan kebijaksanaan politik dengan mengekalkan majoriti melalui perundingan berterusan antara komponen PH-BN. Pendekatan inklusif ini justeru mengukuhkan daya tahan kerajaan. 4.	Walaupun terdapat tanggapan bahawa UMNO sedang dalam proses kebangkitan semula dan berpotensi mengambil alih kuasa, data sebaliknya menunjukkan parti tersebut masih menghadapi cabaran besar. Dalam PRU-15, UMNO hanya berjaya memenangi 26 kerusi berbanding 54 kerusi pada 2018, jelas menunjukkan kemerosotan pengaruhnya dalam kalangan pengundi. 5.	Selain itu, peralihan Tengku Zafrul ke PKR pula dilihat sebagai pengukuhan kepada parti pemerintah itu, di mana beliau membawa bersama pengalaman ekonomi dan jaringan sokongan baharu yang memberi nilai tambah. UMNO masih berada dalam fasa pemulihan pasca-skandal 1MDB dan pengaruhnya dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan kini adalah terhad. 6.	Kerajaan Perpaduan telah menunjukkan komitmennya dalam melaksanakan pelbagai inisiatif reformasi. Antaranya termasuklah pelaksanaan National Anti-Corruption Plan (NACP) dan pemantauan rapi terhadap projek mega seperti LCS, yang membuktikan kesungguhan kerajaan dalam memperkukuh tadbir urus dan ketelusan.  7.	Dalam pada itu, keputusan mahkamah berkenaan kes Datuk Seri Ahmad Zahid Hamidi pula perlu dilihat sebagai proses keadilan yang berasingan daripada pengaruh politik, sekali gus mengukuhkan prinsip pengasingan kuasa dalam sistem demokrasi negara. 8.	Kerajaan Perpaduan di bawah kepimpinan Datoâ€™ Seri Anwar Ibrahim tetap stabil dengan komitmen terhadap tadbir urus baik dan perpaduan nasional. Naratif "krisis kerajaan" dan "kebangkitan UMNO" lebih bersifat retorik politik berbanding realiti semasa. Sebagai kerajaan pertama yang menggabungkan PH-BN-GPS, model ini mencerminkan kematangan demokrasi Malaysia yang terus berkembang. #MyCommunityNews #MCN #KerajaanPerpaduan #AnalisisPolitikSemasa

EGO SEORANG RAFIZI Usai kekalahan pada pemilihan jawatan Timbalan Presiden Parti Keadilan Rakyat pada MPP PKR 2025, Rafizi Ramli mengambil keputusan untuk melepaskan jawatannya sebagai Menteri Ekonomi pula. Pelepasan jawatan itu tidak kosong, turut disertai dengan kenyataan-kenyataan Rafizi, baik secara verbal mahupun bertulis mengenai misi dan visinya menyertai politik sebelum ini- membudayakan 'kebertanggungjawaban mandat rakyat'. Kata Rafizi, ini amalan demokrasi. Bila dah tak dapat sokongan dalam parti, maka secara automatiknya mandat yang sebelum ini digalas turut terkubur. Rafizi dan kenyataan yang berbaur ego! Mungkin Rafizi tak sedar, sebelum ni yang dia katakan sebagai 'mandat rakyat' itu dia dapatkan dengan cara licik dan tak masuk akal. Rafizi galak menghasilan sejumah 'formula-formula aneh' bagi mempengaruhi minda masyarakat untuk menolak hukum logik berlandaskan hakikat, serta kemampuan negara dan kerajaan yang mentadbir. Jika tidak, masakan Rafizi mendapat gelaran 'Raja Formula'? Sudah la bermain dengan formula yang melawan hukum akal. Apabila dipersoalkan kembali sejauh mana keberkesanan formula-formula ini, pasti individu itu akan dikritik hebat oleh Rafizi sendiri! Jawab Rafizi, "Mereka tak faham apa yang saya katakan" atau  "mereka tidak sepandai saya". Tapi tak ada yang lebih hebat apabila Rafizi memberikan reaksi, "Memang bahalol, formula sedang berjalan la bodoh!" Begitukah caranya seorang pemimpin 'bertanggungjawab ke atas mandat rakyat?' Menghina dan memperlekeh, itulah wajah sebenar Rafizi Ramli. Maka tak hairanlah jika dia tak mampu bertahan pada pemilihan kali ini. Rafizi, anda jatuh akibat sikap sendiri! Tapi satu hal yang wajar dipuji. Bila Rafizi tahu dia dah tak ada tempat, baik dalam parti mahu pun dalam kerajaan... Tak tunggu lama, cepat-cepat dia angkat kaki. Tapi tak tahulah kan, drama apa pula Rafizi akan bawa selepas ini. #MyCommunityNews #MCN #RajaFormula #RafiziRamli #EgoSeorangRafizi

[KiniNews] Zaid Ibrahim has urged PAS to exhaust all avenues to court former PKR deputy president Rafizi Ramli and proposed that the party field him in Tambun - the parliamentary seat in Perak held by Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahim.

The ex-law minister also encouraged the Islamist party to approach former PKR vice-president Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad, suggesting that he contest in Bentong, which is DAP MP Young Syefura Othmanâ€™s seat.

â€œBoth are good leaders, and any political party will find them helpful. PAS should try to persuade them to be their candidates for the next general election," he said.

Meanwhile, in a separate story, The Kuala Lumpur High Court has denied Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahimâ€™s bid to suspend the civil lawsuit brought by Yusoff Rawther, who has accused him of sexual assault.

In delivering her ruling today, High Court judge Roz Mawar Rozain also stated that the court had found the eight constitutional questions Anwar had sought to refer to the Federal Court did not meet the required threshold.

Anwar has clarified that it was not about seeking personal immunity, but to ensure that high public office is protected from litigation that may be strategically timed, politically motivated, or institutionally disruptive.

Bekas Timbalan Presiden PKR, Rafizi Ramli, hari ini berkongsi pandangannya mengenai cara membuat keputusan dalam kehidupan seharian, di tengah-tengah spekulasi mengenai hala tuju politiknya selepas tewas dalam pemilihan parti baru-baru ini. â€œKita buat macam-macam keputusan setiap hari, ada keputusan besar, ada keputusan kecil. Petua saya dalam membuat keputusan: Bukan mengenai apa yang kita mahu, tetapi mengenai apa yang perlu dilakukan,â€ katanya dalam satu hantaran di media sosial. Rafizi yang meletak jawatan sebagai Menteri Ekonomi selepas tewas dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, masih belum mendedahkan perancangannya. Belum dapat dipastikan apakah hantaran terbaru itu ada kaitan dengan kerjaya politiknya atau sekadar luahan biasa. Rafizi dalam satu hantaran di platform X minggu lalu berkata beliau akan berkongsi mengenai perancangannya selepas sambutan Hari Raya Aidiladha yang dijangka jatuh pada 7 Jun. Dalam satu hantaran di X minggu lalu, Rafizi berkata: â€œSaya dah rancang apa nak fokus lepas ini, tapi beri masa semua orang bertenang dulu, dengan sambutan Hari Raya Haji dan sebagainya.â€ â€œApa-apa saya kongsi kemudian. Potensi sebenar negara adalah rakyat biasa. Kita perlu kembali bangunkan potensi itu.â€ Dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, Rafizi tewas kepada Nurul Izzah, anak kepada perdana menteri dan Presiden PKR, Anwar Ibrahim. Penyertaan Nurul Izzah dalam pemilihan parti itu telah menimbulkan dakwaan berlakunya amalan nepotisme dalam PKR. Bagaimanapun, Anwar menafikan dakwaan tersebut dan menegaskan bahawa proses pemilihan dijalankan secara demokratik serta terbuka kepada semua ahli parti. Nurul Izzah, anak kepada Presiden PKR merangkap Perdana Menteri, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim, memperoleh 9,803 undi daripada kira-kira 15,000 perwakilan yang mengundi secara fizikal dan dalam talian.
------------------------------

Potensi sebenar negara adalah rakyat biasa. Kita perlu kembali bangunkan potensi itu,â€Dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, Rafizi tewas kepada Nurul Izzah, anak kepada perdana menteri dan Presiden PKR, Anwar Ibrahim.Langkah Nurul Izzah menyertai persaingan merebut jawatan nombor dua dalam PKR itu menimbulkan dakwaan PKR mengamalkan nepotisme.Anwar menafikan dakwaan itu dan menegaskan Nurul Izzah dipilih secara demokrasi oleh ahli parti.Nurul Izzah memperoleh 9,803 undi daripada kira-kira 15,000 perwakilan yang mengundi secara fizikal dan dalam talian

Komen Pembaca
- Segala komen yang dilontarkan oleh pembaca melalui akaun masing-masing adalah pandangan peribadi mereka sendiri. Segala risiko dan akibat yang terhasil melalui komen tersebut adalah tanggungan dan bebanan mereka sendiri.

Komen Pembaca
- Segala komen yang dilontarkan oleh pembaca melalui akaun masing-masing adalah pandangan peribadi mereka sendiri. Segala risiko dan akibat yang terhasil melalui komen tersebut adalah tanggungan dan bebanan mereka sendiri.

Komen Pembaca
- Segala komen yang dilontarkan oleh pembaca melalui akaun masing-masing adalah pandangan peribadi mereka sendiri. Segala risiko dan akibat yang terhasil melalui komen tersebut adalah tanggungan dan bebanan mereka sendiri.

Komen Pembaca
- Segala komen yang dilontarkan oleh pembaca melalui akaun masing-masing adalah pandangan peribadi mereka sendiri. Segala risiko dan akibat yang terhasil melalui komen tersebut adalah tanggungan dan bebanan mereka sendiri.

SHAH ALAM - Muar MP Syed Saddiq Syed Abdul Rahman believes that a person's political journey is long and not defined by a single political cycle.  His comments come after the recent resignations of Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli and Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad.    Syed Saddiq, who is well aware of the unpredictable nature of politics, spoke about the enduring nature of political careers and the importance of continued public service, regardless of formal titles.  â€œThat is their choice and I respect it. He pointed out that political careers are rarely straightforward or confined to one election or term.  "A person's political journey is usually very long. Itâ€™s not just defined by one political cycle.  "From the bottom of my heart, I wish them all the best. Wherever they go, whether in or out of government, Iâ€™m confident theyâ€™ll find the best ways to serve the interests of all Malaysians," he added.  When asked about perceptions of nepotism or internal party dynamics within PKR, Syed Saddiq chose not to comment in detail but reflected on his own experiences.  â€œIâ€™m not going to speak about nepotism or such issues, thatâ€™s an internal party matter. But I can speak from my own personal experience in 2018,â€ he said.  Recalling his time working alongside then-Deputy Prime Minister Datuk Seri Dr Wan Azizah Wan Ismail, Syed Saddiq addressed earlier allegations suggesting she was simply a "seat warmer" for her husband, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim.  â€œIn 2018, there were allegations saying that the then-Deputy Prime Minister, Wan Azizah, was only there because of Datuk Seri Anwar. On May 28, Rafizi officially resigned as Economy Minister, following his defeat in the PKR party elections, stating he no longer had a mandate to continue advancing the partyâ€™s agenda in the government.  Shortly after, Nik Nazmi announced his resignation as Natural Resources and Environmental Sustainability Minister, effective July 4, citing his loss in the PKR elections and noting that his Cabinet role was closely tied to his former position as a party vice president.

Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR) perlu segera membina semula kekuatan pasca-pemilihan peringkat pusat bagi mengukuhkan keyakinan rakyat terhadap parti.

Itu pendapat dua srikandi KEADILAN, saudari Yong Bazilah Abu Bakar dan saudari Siti Aishah Shaik Ismail. Mereka turut merasakan ada ruang untuk yang kalah, seperti bekas Timbalan Presiden, Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli, untuk terus berbakti kepada parti dan negara.

Episod ini dihoskan oleh saudara Daniel Teoh.

This article first appeared in The Edge Malaysia Weekly on May 26, 2025 - June 1, 2025THE European Investment Bank (EIB), the lending arm of the European Union (EU), is keen to participate in more infrastructure-related investments in Malaysia and is open to expanding its reach here.

According to sources, EIB is currently in discussions with the Ministry of Finance (MoF) to set up a legal framework to expand activity in the country, particularly in the Johor-Singapore Special Economic Zone (JS-SEZ).

When contacted, an EIB spokesperson confirms the bank is open to exploring investment opportunities in Malaysia. However, the bank rules out any immediate plans for a dedicated EIB office in Kuala Lumpur, and will maintain its operations at its regional hub in Jakarta.

The EIB, which is one of the worldâ€™s largest multilateral financial institutions, opened its regional representation office for Southeast Asia and the Pacific in Jakarta in September 2022.

The EIB spokesperson emphasised that formalising a country framework agreement would be a critical first step towards establishing the legal basis for EIBâ€™s operations in Malaysia.

â€œOnce such an agreement is in place, we would be pleased to engage with both public and private sector stakeholders to explore and develop a pipeline of potential investments,â€ the spokesperson says.

The move aligns with the EUâ€™s ambitious Global Gateway strategy, which aims to boost smart, clean and secure links in the digital, energy and transport sectors, and to strengthen health, education and research systems worldwide. EIB typically focuses its financing on projects in sustainable infrastructure, the green energy transition, climate resilience, digitalisation and innovation.

Depending on the sector and project readiness, EIB says its investments can range from long-term sovereign or municipal lending to direct financing or intermediated loans through partner banks, particularly for private sector initiatives that contribute to the green and digital transitions.

â€œMalaysia is an important partner for the EU,â€ the EIB spokesperson says. â€œAs the bank of the EU, we are open to engaging with Malaysian authorities to explore opportunities for future collaboration.â€

In April, the EU ambassador to Malaysia Rafael Daerr expressed interest in future funding support via loans, grants or financial guarantees as well as potential EIB investments for the Lumut Maritime Industrial City (LuMIC) in Perak.

â€œThat decision has not been finalised, but the LuMIC project aligns with the EUâ€™s goals under our Global Gateway strategy. It has the potential to become a high-standard, mutually beneficial gateway between Malaysia and Europe,â€ Daerr reportedly said at the LuMIC Masterplan launch on April 10.

The LuMIC project â€” one of Perakâ€™s five regional growth nodes identified under the Perak Sejahtera 2030 blueprint â€” has completed early-stage feasibility and spatial studies, funded by a â‚¬1.9 million (RM9.2 million) grant from EU.

Daerr also mentioned discussions between EIB and MoF for the bank to set up a framework in the country.

Presently, there are several European banks in the country, including Deutsche Bank and BNP Paribas. Deutsche Bank has been operating in Malaysia for over 55 years, with offices in Kuala Lumpur and Labuan, its website shows. BNP Paribas has a locally incorporated subsidiary, BNP Paribas Malaysia Bhd.

While MoF has yet to respond to The Edgeâ€™s queries as at press time, Minister of Economy Datuk Seri Mohd Rafizi Ramli last week hinted at ongoing discussions with a â€œEuropean bankâ€ to attract investments for JS-SEZ.

â€œWe have one European bank that we have been talking to for a while. I think they will come on board. They have been working with us. Itâ€™s just that I think it takes slightly longer to go through the internal process, so the banks will plan and will develop their own programme themselves,â€ Rafizi said during his keynote address at the JS-SEZ Partnersâ€™ Dialogue: Advancing Facilitation session on May 19.

At the event, six major local and international banks signed letters of intent with the Ministry of Economy to help bring investments to JS-SEZ. A total of RM2.35 billion in investment interest had already been secured. The signatories were Malayan Banking Bhd (KL:MAYBANK), CIMB Group Holdings Bhd (KL:CIMB), CGS International, Sumitomo Mitsui Banking Malaysia, Bank of America Malaysia and HSBC Malaysia.

Rafizi said the banks will realise the vision of JS-SEZ through financing support, promotion, stakeholder engagement and market intelligence. He noted that the lenders will have direct access to government policy and support to convince their clients to invest in the zone. The banks were picked to ensure broad international investor outreach, with CGS International targeting Chinese investors, Sumitomo Mitsui covering East Asia, and Bank of America representing the US market, he said.

Nama Datuk Seri Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz kini hangat diperkatakan dalam arena politik Selangor apabila seorang aktivis Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR), Fairul al-Qasas tampil memuji kredibilitiÂ  beliau dan menyifatkannya sebagai tokoh paling layak untuk diangkat sebagai Menteri Besar negeri itu. Kewibawaan Tengku Zafrul sudah terbukti Memetik laporan daripada Malaysia Gazette, Fairul yang juga bekas Ketua Penerangan Cabang PKR Kuala Krau menyatakan kewibawaan beliau sudah terbukti sepanjang memegang jawatan sebagai Menteri Perdagangan, Pelaburan dan Industri (MITI), malah turut mendapat pengiktirafan daripada Perdana Menteri sendiri, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim. â€œPersoalan sama ada beliau mahu diangkat sebagai MB Selangor atau jadi calon PKR PRU-16 tidak sepatutnya jadi isu,â€Â ujarnya. Penyertaan Tengku Zafrul dianggap tepat Tambahnya lagi, penyertaan Tengku Zafrul ke dalam PKR juga dilihat tepat pada masanya dan dibuat dengan cara yang betul â€“ bukan untuk mengejar jawatan, tetapi sebagai langkah menyumbang secara berstruktur dalam parti. â€œKemasukan beliau juga sesuai kerana dibuat selepas pemilihan PKR yang bermakna beliau tidak berhasrat merebut jawatan. â€œJika beliau bertanding dalam pemilihan Keadilan 2028 nanti bermaksud beliau sudah tiga tahun dalam parti dan melepasi tempoh yang ditetapkan,â€Â katanya lagi. Desas-desus Tengku Zafrul jadi MB Selangor semakin kencang Desas-desus mengenai potensi Tengku Zafrul menjadi Menteri Besar Selangor semakin kencang susulan pengumuman beliau meninggalkan UMNO dan menyatakan hasrat menyertai PKR. Ini ditambah pula dengan fakta bahawa tempoh beliau sebagai Senator akan berakhir awal Disember ini. MB Selangor nadi kosongkan kerusi DUN Walau bagaimanapun, Menteri Besar Selangor sedia ada, Datuk Seri Amirudin Shari semalam tampil menafikan akan berlaku kekosongan kerusi DUN Sungai Tua dalam masa terdekat bagi memberi laluan kepada individu tertentu bertanding. Dalam pada itu, Fairul percaya langkah politik Tengku Zafrul telah dirancang lebih awal dan berkemungkinan besar mendapat restu pemimpin kanan kedua-dua parti utama dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan. â€œMaka, ia juga memberi ruang Anwar untuk melantik menteri baharu bersama dua kekosongan menteri yang ditinggalkan Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad,â€Â katanya. Walaupun menyambut baik penghijrahan Tengku Zafrul ke dalam PKR, Fairul mengingatkan agar parti itu kekal menjadi wadah inklusif untuk rakyat dan tidak berubah menjadi eksklusif untuk golongan elit semata-mata. Dalam masa sama, beliau turut menyarankan agar wakil daripada UMNO diberi ruang mengisi kekosongan di MITI bagi mengekalkan kestabilan dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan yang dibina bersama. Sumber:Â Malaysia GazetteÂ (Khuzairi Ismail)

DATUK Seri Tengku Zafrul perlu melepaskan jawatan daripada Kabinet apabila beliau membuat keputusan keluar dari UMNO dan menyertai PKR. Pengarah Lajnah Undang-Undang dan Hak Asasi Manusia (LUHAM) Pas Selangor, Yusfarizal Yussoff berkata, tindakan Tengku Zafrul itu boleh dianggap sebagai lompat parti kerana kedudukan beliau dalam Kabinet adalah atas kapasiti UMNO    Katanya, jelas dari sudut moral politik beliau telah keluar daripada Umno, iaitu parti yang mencadangkannya untuk dilantik sebagai senator dan menteri.   â€œMaka keluarnya daripada Umno bermaksud, beliau sudah tidak mewakili Umno di dalam kerajaan minoriti Perpaduan tersebut,â€ ujar pengamal undang-undang itu,â€ katanya. Yusfarizal mengulas isu-isu semasa berkaitan kedudukan menteri kabinet, antaranya Menteri Ekonomi, Datuk Seri Mohd Rafizi Ramli, dan Menteri Pelaburan, Perdagangan dan Industri, Tengku Datuk Seri Zafrul Abdul Aziz. WAWANCARA | Berdepan pemilihan parti pada muktamar tahun ini, PAS diminta mengelakkan sebarang pertembungan tajam di peringkat tertinggi yang berisiko memberi kesan negatif kepada parti.Berkongsi pandangan peribadi, Naib Presiden PAS Mohd Amar Abdullah berkata, jika Presiden PAS Abdul Hadi Awang memilih untuk berundur sekali pun, posisi itu mesti diganti oleh timbalannya.Pun begitu, Mohd Amar berkata, pada pandangannya pilihan terbaik ialah mengekalkan Abdul Hadi bersama Tuan Ibrahim Tuan Man selaku timbalan presiden.Apa yang perlu dilakukan, kata bekas timbalan Menteri Besar Kelantan itu lagi, PAS perlu â€˜menyusunâ€™ keanggotaan di peringkat ahli Jawatankuasa PAS Pusat supaya semua kebolehan yang ada â€“ iaitu tokoh agamawan, profesional dan teknokrat â€“ dapat digabungkan.â€œSebabnya, (jika gabungan itu wujud) banyak perkara boleh dibincangkan dalam mesyuarat PAS Pusat. Di situlah mereka boleh berikan input-input berkaitan."Di peringkat naib presiden pun dah comel gabungan antara ulama dan bukan ulama. Justeru kita perkemas di peringkat ahli jawatankuasa.â€œYang pimpinan atas biar kekal, itu pandangan saya."Dan kalaulah kalau Tok Guru (Abdul Hadi) kata nak berundur, bagi saya, timbalan kena naik. Jangan ada orang lain nak pintas sebab struktur (parti) kita dah begitu.â€œKalau buat begitu, nampak tenang dalam parti,â€ katanya dalam sesi wawancara bersama Malaysiakini di Kota Bharu, semalam.Dakwa cuba â€˜langgar presidenâ€™Mohd Amar yang juga Adun Panchor menjelaskan kalau ada pertembungan di peringkat jawatan tertinggi, akan ada kesan kepada PAS, khususnya kerana setiap orang mempunyai pengikut tersendiri.Kumpulan yang kalah, katanya, akan berasa tidak puas hati dan mungkin ada â€œmacam-macamâ€ cerita yang keluar.Kerana itu, katanya, dia cenderung agar tiada pertembungan berlaku di peringkat atasan parti.Terdahulu Mohd Amar diminta mengulas mengenai pertandingan dan pertembungan tajam mungkin berlaku dalam Muktamar PAS Ke-72 yang akan berlangsung pada Sept nanti.Walaupun kelihatan bahang pemilihan itu tidak ketara berbanding parti lain, beberapa petanda menunjukkan wujud dua aliran yang sedang bersaing dalam parti tersebut.Misalnya ada pemimpin Pemuda PAS negeri yang menggunakan label â€œkumpulan pro-DAPâ€ kepada pihak tertentu dalam parti berkenaan. Kumpulan yang menggelarkan diri mereka Geng Ustaz pula baru-baru ini membangkitkan isu adanya cubaan â€œmelanggar presidenâ€ dan menganggapnya sebagai â€œkudis lamaâ€ dalam parti tersebut.Malah Presiden Geng Ustaz, Ahmad Dusuki Abd Rani, turut menggelar pihak yang mengganggu kepimpinan ulama sebagai â€œsyaitan-syaitan dalam kalangan manusia dan jinâ€. Mohd Amar menegaskan, kepimpinan PAS memang sejak dulu tidak pernah mengawal atau menyekat sebarang pertandingan dalam parti selagi ia melalui proses dan kelayakan yang ditetapkan perlembagaan.Takkan boleh duduk diamDitanya mengenai kenyataan-kenyataan yang dilihat menggesa agar dua jawatan tertinggi PAS tidak diisi tokoh profesional, Mohd Amar berkata, perkara itu hanya pandangan peribadi pelbagai pihak apabila pemilihan tiba.Pada masa sama lepasan Universiti Birmingham di UK itu juga cenderung agar dua jawatan tertinggi PAS diisi oleh dua tokoh agamawan atau ulama.â€œBiasalah dalam parti memang tiada sebarang halangan. Cuma apabila nak bertanding orang ini ada pandangan, orang itu ada pandangannya, saya pun beri pandangan saya... tapi bukan arahan, sebaliknya sekadar pandangan peribadi,â€ katanyaPun begitu, Mohd Amar mengingatkan, sudah lama PAS tidak menyaksikan pertandingan di peringkat atasan parti itu kerana biasanya ramai yang menarik diri walaupun dicalonkan.Kecuali, katanya, jika ada kekosongan apabila penyandang berundur.Mohd Amar turut akui betapa pertembungan dalam pemilihan akan menyebabkan berlaku pergeseran dalaman seperti yang sedang dialami PKR susulan persaingan di antara Nurul Izzah Anwar dan Rafizi Ramli baru-baru ini.Katanya, pertembungan antara dua pimpinan PKR itu sangat serius dalam konteks politik semasa sekali gus menyaksikan wujud ketidakstabilan politik dalam parti-parti kerajaan Madani.Malah Mohd Amar melihat konflik itu memberi kesan besar kepada negara dan sempat mendoakan agar perwakilan PRK memenangkan Nurul Izzah kerana akan menguntungkan PAS."Masalah Nurul Izzah dan Rafizi ini (isu) besar dari segi politik kerana ia bukan sekadar pertembungan biasa melibatkan anak presiden. â€œSebelum pertandingan saya doakan Nurul Izzah menang, sebab ia bagi kesan perpecahan besar."Rafizi seorang yang loose cannon, (apabila kalah) takkan duduk diam, dia akan terus membedil hingga PRU akan datang. Ini satu kelebihan kepada kita sebagai pembangkang,â€ katanya.Begitu juga DAP apabila Mohd Amar mentafsirkan berlaku pertembungan di antara kem Setiausaha Agung DAP, Anthony Loke, dengan veteran parti itu yang kini menjadi penasihat, Lim Guan Eng.Dalam Umno pula, kata Speaker DUN Kelantan itu lagi, konflik tidak terkecuali sehingga membawa kepada langkah Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz meninggalkan parti berkenaan dan memohon menyertai PKR.â€œSemua ini â€“ kalau orang yang faham politik â€“ akan nampak kelemahan parti-parti tersebut."Sebab itu PAS kena jaga, jangan kita buat perangai serupa (hingga) bertembung tak tentu pasal sesama kita. â€œKalau kita boleh tampilkan imej yang stabil, tenang, tidak berebut jawatan dan tiada kepentingan peribadi, kitalah pilihan terbaik untuk rakyat," jelasnya

Kredit Gambar : UTUSAN TV Strategi Tersirat dan Pergolakan Dalam: Memahami Dinamika Pemilihan PKRPemilihan Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR) yang berlangsung baru-baru ini bukan sekadar medan pertandingan jawatan, tetapi telah membuka tirai kepada satu babak politik dalaman yang penuh dengan perancangan strategik, pertarungan pengaruh dan percaturan masa depan. Apa yang kelihatan sebagai pertandingan biasa sebenarnya menyembunyikan naratif lebih kompleksâ€”naratif yang berkait rapat dengan masa depan kepimpinan parti, penyusunan kuasa dalaman, dan hala tuju kerjasama politik menjelang Pilihan Raya Umum akan datang. Dari Rafizi vs Saifuddin ke Rafizi vs â€œBayanganâ€ Pada awalnya, tumpuan pemilihan tertumpu kepada potensi pertembungan antara Rafizi Ramli dan Setiausaha Agung PKR, Datuk Seri Saifuddin Nasution Ismail, bagi jawatan Timbalan Presiden. Namun, apabila Presiden PKR, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim, mengusulkan agar dua jawatan tertinggi â€“ Presiden dan Timbalan Presiden â€“ tidak dipertandingkan, ramai menjangkakan Rafizi akan meneruskan peranannya tanpa cabaran. Suasana kelihatan tenang di permukaan, namun gelora mula dirasai di bawah arus.Apa yang berlaku selepas itu lebih menarik. Secara tiba-tiba, satu gelombang sokongan yang mengusul agar Nurul Izzah Anwar bertanding untuk jawatan Timbalan Presiden mula muncul di pelbagai cabang PKR di seluruh negara. Kenyataan demi kenyataan daripada akar umbi menyatakan sokongan terbuka kepada beliau walhal sebelum ini, hanya nama Saifuddin yang dipetik oleh media dan dianggap oleh ahli-ahli PKR sendiri sebagai satu-satunya saingan kepada Rafizi sebagai calon Timbalan Presiden. Yang lebih menarik adalah sokongan kepada Nurul Izzah ini secara jelas bukan sesuatu yang berlaku secara spontan,n, tetapi muncul secara serentak dan teratur- seolah-olah kesemua ini adalah perancangan teliti oleh satu gerakan tersusun di belakang tabir. Ini kerana UMNO? Mengapa Nurul Izzah? Mengapa sekarang? Menurut pemerhatian peribadi dan juga berdasarkan info dalaman, Rafizi dikatakan kurang bersetuju dengan cadangan kerjasama erat antara PKR dan UMNO dalam menghadapi PRU akan datang. Walaupun Pakatan Harapan (PH) telah membentuk kerajaan bersama Barisan Nasional (BN), Rafizi kekal berhati-hati. Beliau melihat risiko jangka panjang terhadap identiti politik reformis PKR jika terlalu akrab dengan UMNO, sebuah parti yang suatu ketika dahulu menjadi musuh utama perjuangan reformasi. Pandangan ini tidak semestinya selari dengan strategi politik Anwar yang lebih pragmatikâ€”mencari jalan kembali berkuasa. Tafsiran umum adalah Rafizi telah menyusun rangkaian pengaruhnya dalam Majlis Pimpinan Pusat (MPP) dengan individu-individu yang sealiran dengannyaâ€”satu langkah yang dilihat sesetengah pihak sebagai penguasaan berpusat yang mungkin mengganggu sebarang keputusan yang bakal diambil kelak berkenaan kerjasama bersama UMNO/BN. Pergolakan Kabinet dan Dinamika KepimpinanDalam masa yang sama, spekulasi mengenai rombakan kabinet turut menambah rencah dalam naratif ini. Nama Menteri Besar Selangor, Datuk Seri Amirudin Shari dikaitkan dengan cadangan untuk dilantik sebagai Menteri Perdagangan Antarabangsa dan Industri (MITI), menggantikan Tengku Zafrul Aziz. Pelantikan ini dilihat akan menggugat kedudukan Rafizi sebagai Menteri paling kanan di dalam PKR selepas Anwar Ibrahim. Ini kerana sekiranya Amruddin dilantik sebagai Menteri MITI, Amiruddin akan muncul menyaingi Rafizi sebagai Menteri Kanan dengan portfolio yang penting di dalam kabinet. Malah, ada yang mungkin berpandangan portfolio MITI lebih berprestij daripada portfolio ekonomi bawah Rafizi,  Akhir sekali, sekiranya tafsiran politik saya betul, Nurul Izaah akan mengambil alih sebagai Menteri Besar Selangor dalam strategi yang saya beri nama Langkah Kajang 2.0. Langkah Kajang 2.0 ini bukan sahaja dijangka membuka ruang kepada Nurul Izzah menonjol sebagai pemimpin wanita yang memegang jawatan tertinggi dalam pentadbiran negeri paling maju di Malaysia. Percaturan ini dilakukan untuk mengukir imej Nurul Izzah sebagai pemimpin diterima calon Perdana Menteri kelak. Image credit: MSNIn the last two years since I have been writing about politics professionally, I have met a handful of politicians â€“ two of them are a Dato Seri and one is was a former academic â€“ and I must say that the experience of meeting them was so banal and underwhelming, that I decided to not meet the fourth politicians who I had messaged, and have decided against meeting any politicians ever since.I remember that after meeting one of the politicians, I met my friend for a Teh Tarik, who asked me how did the meeting with the politician go ?I remember how I answered him. I told him that having Teh Tarik with him was a far more enlightening and insightful experience.The reason that that I find talking to a regular person is more enlightening and insightful than talking to all of the politicians that I have met, is that all the politicians I have met, without fail, were not at all focused-on reality, but on how to make me see them as how they wanted to me to see them.Politicians, in other words, are focused almost entirely on your perception of them, and not at all on the realities of the world.Because of that, when I talk to a politician, I found the conversation to be insipid, insightful and banal, even when the politicians were doing their best to speak in the most bombastic manner, simply because talking to them never makes you feel that you understand reality better.All it will make you do is think about the politician that you are talking to â€“ about how smart, righteous, powerful, selfless, deep and awesome they are â€“ and I found the experience to be a waste of time, because I generally only like to think about women, not old men.Comparatively, when you talk to regular people, they will often give you a greater insight about reality, because their mind is often in tune with the realities that they deal with.  If you want to know what the problem with the roads are, for example, talk to a lorry driver, who will not only explain to you why a problem with the road is a problem, he might even have a practical and cost-effective way of addressing the problem.The reason I am bringing up this subject is because in the first message that Rafizi released after he resigned, he said that he has a plan, and a big part of the plan entails taking politics back to the people.â€œI do have plans on what I want to focus on, but I want to wait for the situation to cool off.â€œThe countryâ€™s real potential is the public. We have to go back to harnessing this potential,â€ Rafizi said on X.I heartily agree with this idea because I think politics is indeed best when it is regular people, who deal with the realities of life on a daily basis, participate in it, rather than the elites or a career politician, who other than manufacture your perception of him or her, is probably a person that is ill equipped to deal with reality.If you think about when politics was best in the country, you will probably see that it was best during the early days of independence, when it was mostly just regular people, who were very in tune with the realities of the world, that participated in politics. It is when regular people participated in politics that practical, insightful and effective ideas were turned into policies, which in turn powered the country forward.The problem with grassroot politics tends to be its own success â€“ grassroot politics only comes about a big problem arises, like how the return to colonial rule enabled the condition to activate grassroot politics in the independence era -  but once the grassroot politics become successful, as our own independence era grassroot politics became successful, because it not only achieved independence for the nation, it managed to lift the masses into the country out of poverty, backwardness and illiteracy within just a couple of decades,  it will becomes institutionalised, and once it is institutionalised, it is career politicians, who become far removed from the realities of life, that will monopolise the political space in the country.Career politicians,  who participate in politics for politics sake, are almost invariably people who are focused on forming your opinion of them, or building an image, rather than someone who is focused on the realities of the world.These career politicians canâ€™t focus on the realities of the world, not only because most of them have no real-life experience, but because that is not how they have trained their mind. These are people who do not train themselves to ask practical or reality based questions, like whether it is possible to travel from Subang Jaya on a weekday afternoon, make a drop at Sunway and another one at PJ, and return back to Subang Jaya within one and half hours. Instead, these are people who are chiefly focused and trained, to sit, dress, walk and talk in a certain way, and to also to study your expression and reactions, to see whether they have managed to convince you to believe that they know something that they donâ€™t and are capable of something that they are not.The problem with regular people as opposed to politicians, is that regular people tend to be focused on being good, while politicians tend to be focused on winning.To join politics, you have to have the mentality of a winner or a fighter, or someone who enters the arena, together with other people just like them, to fight and defeat as many people as they can, so that you can gain as much power, authority and glory from the arena as possible.Unfortunately, regular people tend to think that this competitive spirit, where you are looking at everybody around you with the intention to fight their weak point so that you can exploit it and defeat them, to be â€œnot goodâ€, and thus they shy away from politics, until their circumstances and realities of life become so bad, that they will be forced to join politics.  If Rafizi truly wishes to take politics back to the people, then maybe he should think of a way to make regular people see politics just as a game â€“ like football â€“ where you do things like argue and criticise others for the same reason that you dribble pass or tackle a person on the football field â€“because it is just the nature of the game to do so and it is fun.For as long as regular people think that to criticise others and argue is something that is â€œnot goodâ€, they will continue to shy away from politics for as long as they can afford to.If we can only get regular people to more actively participate in politics only when the circumstances in the country becomes so bad, it is start to negatively affect the realities of common people, we are doomed to forever be firefighting, or fix a problem only when it becomes really bad, without ever reaching a stage where we will be able to refine ourselves to a finer and more exalted state.If Rafizi can just find a way to get regular people with real life experiences to engage in politics for fun and see it just as a game, perhaps we can create a more dynamic and vibrant political environment, that is focused on reality and intent on generating value, as how the politicians that arose from the grassroot during the Merdeka era created a dynamic, vibrant, reality focused and value generating culture in our politics, which shook off the country of the backwardness, lethargy and the torpor of institutionalised politics, that had infected the land for hundreds of years, and caused to rise again after declining for hundreds of years. This might be one of the very few jobs in Malaysia where your end date is published on the newspapers. Even in the final weeks, however, I still couldnâ€™t explain what I do to others. 

At the Ministry of Economy, I do what the system calls â€œstructural reformsâ€. The easiest way to understand is to see it as redoing an old house. Itâ€™s about looking at what makes the houseâ€”walls, layout, wiring, plumbing, flooringâ€”and keeping what still works, discarding what no longer serves, and being open to a fundamentally new house.

Or you could just see us as the planner for the economy. 

Throughout our time here, weâ€™ve tried to be as intentional in what we do as possible. In speeches, we avoided clichÃ©s and corny platitudes. No jargon, no generalities, no long sentences. Clarity above all. Listeners must understand every word we say and feel like theyâ€™ve learned something, without being talked down. 

In programs, we avoided shortcuts. We cold-called, did decks, and pitched to power players who wouldnâ€™t otherwise know about Malaysia. 

In our â€œstructural reformsâ€, we avoided ribbon-cutting ceremonies that are larger than the policies. Launch ceremonies are to showcase early wins. Major reforms must be rooted in an overriding rationale (see images). 

We couldnâ€™t finish what we started. But policymaking is like writing. It is not about using 1,200 words as the first and final say on a topic, but to say enough so that the next person would know where to pick up in a long conversation. Policymaking, like writing, is about passing the baton. 

I could not have applied for this job, nor could I have prepared for it. But once I have gone through it, I walk out knowing what I never knew (see images).

To every civil servant who made space for this 29-year old to join meetings and lead policiesâ€”try, fail, fix, repeatâ€”I hope God repays your kindness. I could only buy so many chocolates from the airport. To my team who went through the worst of times together: Letâ€™s never do this again. We will forever be cursed with this unbreakable bond and we will never forget this even if we tried our hardest. 

And to Minister Rafizi Ramli whom I have known for 12 years. Everyone who has seen Rafizi as a minister will not question his dedication. Through this experience, I saw his idealism at full display. Only idealism would convince a person to stake everything for his country (heart attack, slipped discs, lost voiceâ€”he always turned up one week after). Above all, he showed me the value that precedes all: Courage. The inexplicable, maddening belief of doing the right thing, even when it is unpopular. Iâ€™ve seen him in many forms. This was his best. Thank you for opening the door for me. 

In all my life, this was the proudest work Iâ€™ve done. Serving my country will always be the greatest honour of my life. Thank you for seeing me on this roller-coaster.

ç°‡ #90 (åŒ…å« 1 æ¡æ–‡æ¡£)
--------------------------------------------------
Factories store CO2 underground or use it in industrial processes as part of CCUS technology (Photo by BLOOMBERG)
Malaysiaâ€™s push for carbon capture technology highlights its potential to cut emissions while raising concerns about safety, costs and environmental risksÂ 
AS NATIONS race toward net-zero targets amid a narrowing window to address climate change, Carbon Capture, Utilisation and Storage (CCUS) is emerging both as a promising technological solution and a focal point of environmental debate.
CCUS is a technology designed to capture carbon dioxide (CO2) from point sources such as factories or directly from the atmosphere. The captured CO2 is then either stored permanently underground or utilised as a feedstock in various industrial processes.
            
            
            
By physically reducing emissions, CCUS enables the creation of value-added products and services that are increasingly accepted in global markets â€” potentially offsetting the costs of adopting the technology.
According to the International Energy Agency (IEA), CCUS is considered a critical tool in achieving global energy and climate goals, particularly for emissions that are technically challenging or prohibitively expensive to eliminate.
In Malaysia, the recent passage of the CCUS Bill in March marks a significant policy shift, paving the way for the large-scale deployment of carbon capture initiatives across key industrial sectors.
While many local experts acknowledge that the bill leaves important questions unanswered â€” especially regarding CCUSâ€™s long-term role in meeting Malaysiaâ€™s climate commitments â€” it is nevertheless seen as a step forward. It represents a flagship catalyst project and a vital component of the National Energ y Transition Roadmap (NETR), aimed at serving countries that seek to use CCUS to lower their carbon emissions.
As the bill awaits further development of implementation guidelines, the debate is intensifying â€” between supporters who view CCUS as essential for addressing hard-to-abate emissions and critics who highlight its substantial financial and environmental costs.
Zapantis explains that CCUS plays a crucial role in cutting emissions, working alongside renewables to tackle sectors with limited alternatives (Source: globalccsinstitute.com)
Critical for Net Zero
Global CCS Institute Strategic Advisor for Emerging CCS (Carbon Capture and Storage) Markets, Alex Zapantis, said while CCUS is not a one-size-fits-all solution, it remains a vital component in the global push toward net-zero emissions â€” particularly in SouthEast Asia (SE Asia).
He stressed that CCUS should not be viewed as a substitute for renewable energy (RE), nuclear power, or energy efficiency improvements. However, it is a crucial technology for industrial sectors where alternative solutions are currently not yet viable.
â€œMost international reports and analyses show that we need to use every tool at our disposal to reach net zero. If we remove any of them from the equation, it becomes more difficult, more expensive and possibly even impossible,â€ he told Bernama.
While hydrogen has been touted as a cleaner alternative for processes like steel production via direct reduced iron (DRI), Zapantis pointed out that clean hydrogen production at commercial scale still often relies on CCS.
â€œTo produce low-emission hydrogen, CCS remains the most cost-effective and scalable method available today,â€ he said.
On the energy front, Zapantis also addressed a common misconception: that CCS competes with RE. He argued that in SE Asiaâ€™s context, the two should be seen as complementary.
â€œWe need as much RE as we can deploy, but there are limits to what the grid can handle due to the intermittent nature of these sources. CCS complements renewables â€” itâ€™s not in competition with them,â€ he added.
Nature-based Solutions
When asked whether nature-based solutions (NbS) â€” such as forests and green carbon sinks â€” could replace CCUS in absorbing CO2, Zapantis said these approaches, while important, have inherent limitations.
â€œNbS plays a vital role in addressing climate change, but they cannot replace CCUS. They are limited by land availability and offer far less security compared to underground carbon storage through CCS,â€ he explained.Â 
Citing findings from the US National Academies of Sciences, Engineering and Medicine, Zapantis noted that the upper limit of effective CO2 abatement through NbS globally is estimated at just five to seven gigatonnes (Gt) per year.
â€œBeyond that threshold, NbS begins to compete with essential needs such as food production, fibre, water and biodiversity. When you consider that global emissions stand at around 40 Gt annually, NbS can only provide a fraction of whatâ€™s required,â€ he said.
Zapantis said that another key challenge with NbS is permanence â€” the durability of carbon storage over time.
â€œCCS offers a more secure form of storage. Thanks to over a century of oil and gas (O&G) operations and decades of geological research, we know that CO2, when stored in a properly selected underground reservoir, remains there.
â€œEven if leakage occurs, it can be detected and remedied with existing O&G technologies,â€ he said.
In contrast, carbon stored in trees or soil is vulnerable to natural and human-induced risks such as wildfires, pests, droughts and land-use changes.
â€œIf those trees are lostâ€”whether due to fire, disease, or logging â€” the carbon is released back into the atmosphere. The risk of reversal is significantly higher compared to CCS,â€ he added.
Zapantis argued that the most effective strategy is to prevent emissions from entering the atmosphere in the first place.
â€œCCUS achieves this by capturing CO2 directly at the source â€” be it a power plant or industrial facility â€” and storing it securely. Thatâ€™s far more effective than emitting carbon and trying to remove or offset it later,â€ he said.
When asked whether CCUS could be misused as a licence to prolong fossil fuel use, Zapantis was firm in his response.
â€œCCUS should be seen as one element of a broader climate strategy that includes renewables, energy efficiency and nature-based solutions. Itâ€™s not about extending the life of fossil fuels. Itâ€™s about managing emissions from hard-to-abate sectors.
â€œIn SE Asia, where energy demand continues to rise and fossil fuels still dominate the energy mix, CCUS is essential to achieving emissions targets,â€ he said.Â 
Theseira raises concerns over the reliability of monitoring technologies for offshore CO2 storage, highlighting potential risks of undetected leaks (Pic courtesy of Dr Gary Theseira)
Safety Matters
While CCUS is being promoted as a key technology to help Malaysia and SE Asia achieve their net-zero targets, concerns persist â€” particularly around the safety and reliability of offshore carbon storage.
Climate policy expert Dr Gary Theseira warned that current monitoring technologies are not yet mature enough to guarantee the secure containment of CO2 injected beneath the seabed. This raises serious questions about the risk of undetected leaks and the long-term liabilities associated with such storage.
â€œAt present, there is no existing technology capable of effectively monitoring the seabed once CO2 is injected offshore.
â€œIf a leak occurs, the gas dissolves into seawater almost immediately, making it virtually untraceable,â€ he told Bernama.
Theseira, who also serves as Chair of the Climate Governance Malaysia Council, noted that NbS are already playing an active role in carbon sequestration.
â€œWe already have forests and natural carbon sinks doing the job. Perhaps we should be channelling more investment and attention into enhancing these systems,â€ he said.
He cited biomass waste â€” such as pruned branches and deadwood â€” as a valuable resource that could be transformed into biochar, a more stable and potentially safer method of carbon sequestration.
â€œFor me, the most promising alternative is biochar. Itâ€™s a form of CCUS, just with a different, more grounded approach â€” and potentially less risky,â€ he said.
(Biochar is a charcoal-like substance produced by burning organic material from agricultural or forestry waste (biomass) in a controlled process known as pyrolysis. Although it resembles common charcoal, biochar is made using a method designed to minimise contamination and securely store carbon over the long term).
Needs a Coherent Policy Framework
Theseira said the government should consider passing the long-delayed National Climate Change Bill (RUUPIN) before advancing the CCUS Bill or implementing a carbon tax.Â 
He warned that without a coherent legal and policy framework, efforts to combat climate change â€” through mechanisms like CCUS and carbon pricing â€” risk becoming fragmented or even counterproductive.
â€œAll of these mechanisms â€” CCUS, carbon tax and broader emissions regulations â€” must align towards the same outcome,â€ he said. â€œOtherwise, we risk different sectors lobbying for conflicting interests, as weâ€™ve already seen in the automotive sector,â€ he said.
On Feb 5, Minister of Natural Resources and Environmental Sustainability Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad said the government is in the process of drafting RUUPIN as part of its broader strategy to achieve net-zero emissions by 2050. He noted that meeting this target would require radical transformations across government, industry and society.
Frustration intensified when Minister of Economy Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli announced that the government aimed to enforce CCUS legislation by March 31 to attract long-term investment opportunities. The accelerated timeline sparked concern that the push for CCUS is being driven more by economic incentives than environmental integrity.
This has led to criticism from environmental NGOs, who argue that Malaysia may be prioritising foreign investment over safety and sustainability. Concerns have also been raised about the countryâ€™s readiness to manage potential risks â€” such as leaks â€” especially if Malaysia begins importing carbon waste for storage.
Risk of Leakage
Sahabat Alam Malaysia (SAM) president Meenakshi Raman has urged the government to address the risk of water contamination from potential leakage at CCUS sites into adjacent geological formations.
She argued that the current CCUS Bill lacks adequate safeguards to protect the environment and public health and called for urgent improvements before Malaysia proceeds with any CCUS project bids.
â€œCCUS projects have been associated with high rates of failure and cancellation. They are also susceptible to significant cost overruns and may result in stranded assets,â€ she said.
Meenakshi referred to a report by a United Nations (UN) Special Rapporteur on the toxic impacts of proposed climate change solutions, which highlighted the chemical intensity of the carbon capture process. According to the report, this process can release substantial quantities of hazardous substances â€” including highly toxic ammonia â€” into surrounding communities.
â€œAt high concentrations, CO2 itself is a toxic gas and an asphyxiant. It can cause circulatory insufficiency, coma and even death,â€ she warned.
She also raised concerns about the lack of inclusive representation in the decision-making process for CCUS implementation.
â€œTo date, civil society and community-based groups have not been included in CCUS agency meetings. All appointments are made at the ministryâ€™s discretion, which-limits transparency, accountability and the diversity of perspectives â€” especially those that may challenge government or industry priorities,â€ she added. â€” BERNAMA

appy-with-countrys-direction-under-anwarhttps://www.iseas.edu.sg/articles-commentaries/iseas-perspective/2024-21-a-deep-dive-into-malaysias-peoples-justice-party-pkr-by-james-chaihttps://www.internationalaffairs.org.au/australianoutlook/malaysian-pm-anwar-ibrahims-dilemma-between-power-and-reform/

Timbalan Presiden PKR, Nurul Izzah Anwar bersama suaminya, Yin Shao Loong dilihat berangkat ke Tanah Suci bagi menunaikan ibadah haji, sekali gus menyempurnakan Rukun Islam kelima. Nurul Izzah dan suami berangkat tunai haji Perkara itu diketahui menerusi satu video yang dikongsi di akaun TikTokÂ Nurul Izzahâ€™s FansÂ pagi ini apabila memuat naik momen pasangan tersebut yang tersenyum dan melambai tangan dipercayai sebelum berangkat ke Mekah. Penyokong doakan Nurul Izzah dan suami peroleh haji mabrur Akaun TikTok berkenaan juga mendoakan agar urusan Nurul Izzah dan suami dipermudah di sana dan mendapat haji yang mabrur. â€œYa Allah, jadikanlah ibadah hajinya sebagai haji yg mabrur, saâ€™inya sebagai usaha yg Engkau terima dan amalannya sebagai amalan soleh yg diterima. Sebelum ini, dalam Kongres Nasional PKR bulan lalu, anak sulung kepada Perdana Menteri Malaysia, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim itu telah menyatakan hasrat untuk menunaikan ibadah haji. Ketika itu, beliau baru sahaja diumum sebagai Timbalan Presiden PKR selepas menewaskan penyandang jawatan, Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli, dalam pemilihan parti pada 23 Mei. Difahamkan, sejurus selesai mengerjakan haji, beliau akan kembali memberi fokus kepada usaha mengukuhkan kerjasama dan hubungan dalam parti, selain memperkemas gerak kerja dalaman PKR menjelang Pilihan Raya Umum ke-16 (PRU16) serta Pilihan Raya Negeri (PRN) Sabah. Image credit: Malay MailNow that Nurul Izzah is the new number 2 of PKR, the question on everybodyâ€™s mind is whether she is going to take a cabinet position.The fact that Rafizi and Nik Nazmi, two PKR heavyweights that lost in the PKR election have resigned from the cabinet, is naturally making everybody wonder whether Nurul Izzah, the biggest winner in the PKR elections, will fill in the cabinet seats that they vacated, and serve also as a government minister.The departure of the two ministers, as well as the recent move by Tengku Zafrul, who is also a minister, to leave Umno and join PKR, will also most likely warrant a cabinet reshuffle, because Umno has already demanded that Tengku Zafrul returns the cabinet position he holds back to Umno, now that he has left Umno.On a lesser note, that Ramanan has emerged as the new and second most popular vice president of PKR, will also possibly mean that Ramanan, who is currently serving as a deputy minister, will be given a full ministerial portfolio.Considering all this, it might be likely that Anwar might use this occasion to revamp the cabinet altogether, and in the new line up, the likelihood that Nurul Izzah might end up with a high level cabinet position, is definitely being speculated heavily amongst the people.Personally, my gut feeling is that Nurul Izzah might be having reservations about taking on a cabinet role.My gut feeling is so, because there is something about her countenance and expressions, that inclines me to believe that she is still a person that is governed by her conscience, and when you are governed by your conscience, your conscience will disturb you, whenever you are contemplating on taking an action, that might not fully satisfy your conscience.She might be contemplating it, despite the reservation from her conscience, because from an intellectual, logical and natural point of view, I am sure that there are 101 reasons to persuade Nurul Izzah to take up a cabinet position.As a matter of instinct, it is human nature to want things such as power, wealth, status and position. Nurul Izzah had won the PKR elections in a fair and square manner. Previously, when she lost the Permatang Pauh seat in the last general election, she had stepped back from party and government position, so logically, and in all fairness, now that she has won a high position the PKR by election, in a fair and square manner, why shouldn't' she aim for a cabinet position?.In this world, it is considered just for the victor to  get the prize â€“this how the world works â€“ considering that she has won the recent PKR election, why should she be denied a prize?Politically speaking, if she takes up a cabinet position, she will also not have to worry about political repercussions. Some analysts are saying that Anwar is facing the â€œultimate testâ€ because of Rafiziâ€™s and Nik Nazmiâ€™s resignation, as well as Tengku Zafrulâ€™s move to leave Umno and join PKR, but I donâ€™t think this is the case at all.I think Anwarâ€™s position today is at the strongest that it has ever been, and now with Nurul Izzah as his deputy, he is even in a stronger position.At the end of the day, people might support the challenger, but they will follow the winner. Either way, what they will definitely avoid like the plague is the losers.Anwar and PH are currently the only dominant winners in the country. A lot of his supporters are getting increasingly disappointed, frustrated and dissatisfied with his reign, but this doesn't change the fact that he is the only dominant winner in the country. The opposition, PN, is nowhere close to matching his lead. Considering that,  regardless of how disappointed, frustrated and dissatisfied his followers are . In the end, they will still follow him.Although I think that Rafiziâ€™s and Nik Nazmi decision to  resign their cabinet position is principled and admirable move, in terms of perception and realpolitik, I feel that their action will likely cause them to be perceived as losers, which means that in the not too distant future, they might  go from the position of strength and relevance that they are in today, to a position of irrelevance and obliviousness.I think whatever tantrum that Umno is throwing over Tengku Zafrulâ€™s move is but a storm in the teacup, or just something that is expected for them to do under the circumstances. Once they have done throwing the tantrum they are expected to throw,  I am quite certain that the supposed â€œoutrageâ€ that they are currently displaying, will thaw and disappear, without making any significant impression in the fabric of reality.Whatever the pundits are saying, I strongly feel that unless something unexpected happens, Anwar and PH are still going to form the ruling government after the next election.So what is the problem with Nurul Izzah taking the cabinet position then, you ask ?Well the problem is that all the explanations I have given, as to why no one can fault Nurul Izzah for taking a cabinet position and no reason why she shouldn't, is the sort of explanation that you would expect from Mahathir's generation. Mahathir always has an explanation for everything â€“ no matter how unconscionable Mahathirâ€™s actions are, logically, legally and intellectually â€“ he is always able to defend his actions and decisions. That is part of the reason why Mahathir has not been found to be guilty of any wrongdoing so far, although much of his reign was filled with scandals and outrage, and despite the fact that is his reign that is usually associated with the descend of the nation into the realms of corruption, exploitation and racial and religious tension.Nurul Izzah is known as the daughter of Reformasi. She herself has claimed that she wishes to carry forth the torch of reformasi.A key goal of reformasi, as we all know, is to dismantle the excesses and degeneracy of the old regime, and a key requirement to dismantle the excesses and degeneracy of the old regime, is to bring the governance by conscience back into the picture.  To bring back the governance of conscience back in to the picture, instead of suppressing one's conscience, with the brute force of oneâ€™s intellectual and logical prowess, one should practise being true to oneself, practise restrain and always make sure that no matter how much one pursues one's self interest, one will not pursue it outside the limits of established principles.When you have a conscience, you can see everybody as yourself, and have a sense of restraint and empathy governing your actions.We all want power, money, fame, wealth and recognition.If you have a conscience, you wonâ€™t fault yourself for wanting things like power, position and wealth, but you will also be able to understand that others, like you, want it too, and thus restrain your desires in such a way, that you will only fulfil your self desire, if you have done something to deserve it. I think it is fair that Nurul Izzah is the new PKR number 2. I think she deserves the number 2 position in PKR. As for a cabinet position, I think she should wait until she wins a by-election or her party wins the next general election, under her command, before she can say that he has deserved it. If she does that, I feel that indeed she will be able to carry the torch of reformasi forward, turn back the excesses of Mahathirism, exorcise the country from the plague of corruption, separatism, racism and exploitation that the old regime has possessed us with, with their degenerate value system, , and return the nation again to the right path, where will once again be a land where the people are able to  pursue of a true and meaningful happiness, both in this life as well as the next.TheRealNehruism (nehru.sathiamoorthy@gmail.com) is a content creator under the Newswav Creator programme, where you get to express yourself, be a citizen journalist, and at the same time monetize your content & reach millions of users on Newswav. Fahmi bercakap pada sidang media selepas Majlis Pelancaran Garis Panduan Etika bagi Pelaporan dan Perkongsian Kandungan Berkaitan Bunuh Diri di Menara Star pada Selasa. Foto BernamaUntuk berita terkini Sinar Harian, ikuti di Telegram dan TikTok kamiPETALING JAYA â€“ Menteri Komunikasi, Datuk Fahmi Fadzil hari ini melancarkan â€œGaris Panduan Pelaporan dan Perkongsian Kandungan Berkaitan Bunuh Diriâ€, yang merupakan inisiatif pertama seumpamanya di dunia, dibangunkan menerusi pendekatan dipacu industri secara inklusif dan melibatkan pelbagai pihak berkepentingan.Fahmi ketika berucap pada majlis pelancaran inisiatif tersebut berkata, usaha proaktif oleh Forum Kandungan Komunikasi dan Multimedia (CMCF) dalam membangunkan garis panduan itu telah menghimpunkan Kementerian Kesihatan, pengamal media dan individu dengan pengalaman hidup sebenar, serta diperkukuh menerusi rundingan awam.â€œMalah, Malaysia telah dijemput untuk membentangkan inisiatif ini di International Association for Suicide Prevention (IASP) World Congress 2025, bulan ini di Vienna, dengan CMCF mewakili negara kita,â€ katanya pada majlis pelancaran garis panduan itu di Menara Star, pada Selasa.Turut hadir, Pengerusi CMCF, Rafiq Razali; Timbalan Ketua Setiausaha (Infrastruktur Telekomunikasi) Kementerian Komunikasi, Mano Verabathran; Timbalan Ketua Pengarah (Kesihatan Awam) Kementerian Kesihatan, Dr Ismuni Bohari; serta Pengerusi Star Media Group (SMG), Tan Sri Wong Foon Meng.Fahmi berkata, Kementerian Komunikasi bersama Suruhanjaya Komunikasi dan Multimedia Malaysia (MCMC) akan terus menyokong usaha seperti itu bagi memastikan ekosistem kandungan di Malaysia kekal selamat, inklusif dan menyokong kesejahteraan rakyat.â€œSaya juga ingin menyeru semua pemain industri sama ada pengamal media, pencipta kandungan, pempengaruh atau pengguna harian untuk merujuk dan mengamalkan garis panduan ini dalam penciptaan serta perkongsian kandungan harian mereka,â€ katanya.Beliau berkata, pelaporan mengenai kes bunuh diri merupakan antara topik yang paling sensitif dan menyayat hati yang dihadapi wartawan, dan amat penting untuk dilaporkan dengan penuh tanggungjawab dan berhemah.â€œIni terutamanya demi pertimbangan serta belas ihsan terhadap keluarga si mati. Terdapat juga fenomena â€˜bunuh diri tiruanâ€™ (copycat suicide), iaitu orang lain yang mengetahui tentang tragedi tersebut cuba menirunya.Artikel Berkaitan: Tiada maklumat mengenai peletakan jawatan Rafizi - Fahmi Fadzil  Garis panduan 2005 masih wujud  Wajar atau tidak tambah baik garis panduan berkaitan umat Islam? â€œAtas dua sebab ini sahaja, kita tidak boleh sesekali mengambil ringan mengenai pelaporan dan perkongsian kandungan berkaitan bunuh diri,â€ katanya.Dalam sidang media, Fahmi berkata, beliau menyambut baik pendekatan TikTok yang secara sukarela menjadi ahli Forum Kandungan.Berita Telus & Tulus menerusi E-Mel setiap hari!NewSinarHarian2020.csvXâ€œFacebook, Instagram dan X masih jauh daripada memuaskan. Saya akan berkomunikasi dengan mereka juga, tetapi mereka perlu faham bahawa Forum Kandungan ini bukan diketuai kerajaan, sebaliknya dipacu industri,â€ katanya.Beliau turut menyeru semua platform agar turut serta membangunkan amalan terbaik dan kod etika demi kepentingan bersama.â€œSaya berharap garis panduan ini diamalkan oleh semua pihak bukan sahaja wartawan, tetapi juga mereka yang membuat pelaporan di lapangan dan dalam seluruh struktur organisasi media.â€œUntuk melakukan perubahan secara menyeluruh, terutama dari segi budaya pelaporan, seluruh organisasi perlu memahami dan menghormati prinsip-prinsip yang digariskan,â€ katanya.Fahmi turut meminta Forum Kandungan menganjurkan bengkel libat urus melibatkan sebanyak mungkin organisasi media di Semenanjung, Sabah dan Sarawak.â€œKita juga perlu libatkan media sosial kerana kandungan berkaitan bunuh diri bukan hanya dilaporkan oleh media, tetapi turut disebarkan di platform mereka,â€ katanya.Menjawab soalan mengenai kecukupan undang-undang bagi mengawal selia media sosial, Fahmi berkata ia bukan hanya isu perundangan tetapi juga melibatkan sikap pengendali platform yang lebih mementingkan keuntungan.â€œSaya baru pulang daripada mesyuarat menteri-menteri komunikasi rantau Asia Pasifik dan dapati banyak negara menghadapi isu serupa berkaitan media sosial,â€ katanya. - BernamaMuat turun aplikasi Sinar Harian. PETALING JAYA: Selangor menteri besar Amirudin Shari has denied speculation that he is set to vacate his Sungai Tua state seat to make way for Tengku Zafrul Aziz to contest in the ensuing by-election, representing PKR. Amirudin said this was just empty talk based on the â€œwild imaginationâ€ of certain individuals who were seeking to spread that narrative via social media, Sinar Harian reported. The PKR vice-president also said he did not want to see a repeat of the â€œKajang Moveâ€ in 2014, which culminated in the late Abdul Khalid Ibrahim resigning as the then Selangor menteri besar. The â€œKajang Moveâ€ refers to PKRâ€™s plan in 2014 to trigger a by-election in the Kajang state seat to install Anwar Ibrahim as the next Selangor menteri besar to replace Khalid, who was seen as going against party policies. The move fizzled out after Anwarâ€™s conviction in his sodomy case was upheld by the Court of Appeal, and eventually led to Azmin Ali being appointed menteri besar. Amirudin said that episode had triggered political uncertainty in Selangor although Khalidâ€™s state government initially had a solid majority in the legislative assembly. â€œI donâ€™t think (I will vacate the seat). I want to complete my term (as menteri besar) in full and ensure harmony because there are a lot of things that we need to settle. â€œThis (speculation) doesnâ€™t need to be prolonged. (PKRâ€™s) focus is on aligning our leadership and the issues related to the cohesion of the federal and state governments, as well as the upcoming Sabah election,â€ he said. Tengku Zafrul, the investment, trade and industry minister, had quit Umno last week and expressed his intention to join PKR. There has been speculation over his fate as minister as his final term as senator expires at the end of the year. Also, there is public expectation of a Cabinet reshuffle as Rafizi Ramli and Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad have quit their ministerial posts. In a Facebook video yesterday, former Umno leader Isham Jalil claimed that Amirudin would be ordered to vacate his Sungai Tua seat to allow Tengku Zafrul to contest in the by-election. Winning the by-election could then allow Tengku Zafrul to take over as menteri besar, as speculated previously, while Amirudin could join Anwarâ€™s Cabinet as he is also the Gombak MP at present.

From Jeffri Saling I read Terence Nettoâ€™s defence of outgoing economy minister Rafizi Ramli with some amusement. He has gone to lengths to portray Rafizi as a gallant hero who stepped down in a valiant effort to stem the tide against those who would compromise the principles of â€œreformasiâ€. While I would never challenge Rafiziâ€™s great contributions to the party and the country, I am also equally sure that they are being exaggerated. How visible was he as economy minister these past two and a half years? What did he really do? Is he really that approachable, because the feedback, even from his supporters, is often that he is aloof. How come his â€œreformasiâ€ principles werenâ€™t offended until he himself tasted defeat in the party polls? This isnâ€™t even the first time he reacted in a churlish manner, taking a step back when his contributions are needed. I wonder how staff members feel about his move, given that he has left them jobless. Given that he is an acclaimed vanguard of the reform movement, is it not immature and irresponsible of him to walk away when he is most needed? Letâ€™s not forget that the party leaders attempted to work with him after the polls. Now he is standing in the corner playing the victim. Does this really help the cause he professes to be fighting for? I fear that Rafizi is closing the door on himself. Â  Jeffri Saling is an FMT reader. Seorang pemimpin PKR didakwa sedang giat menghubungi ketua-ketua cabang bagi meraih sokongan untuk melobi jawatan menteri. Bekas timbalan komunikasi PKR Sabah Fekirie Gobet yang membuat tuduhan itu menggesa pucuk pimpinan parti bertindak segera dan mengeluarkan larangan terhadap amalan ini. "Saya menerima panggilan daripada salah seorang pembantu pemimpin itu. Dia bertanya mengenai Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi (Nik Ahmad). "Semasa perbualan, dia memberitahu saya bahawa pemimpin itu sedang menghubungi ketua-ketua cabang dan beberapa pemimpin dari PKR mengumpul tandatangan untuk menyatakan sokongan kepadanya dilantik sebagai menteri menggantikan Nik," katanya kepada Malaysiakini. Bekas timbalan komunikasi PKR Sabah Fekirie Gobet. Menurut Fekirie, dia menghubungi sendiri beberapa ketua cabang yang memaklumkan menerima panggilan serupa. Katanya, tindakan itu mencabar kuasa presiden PKR yang juga Perdana Menteri Anwar Ibrahim dalam menentukan barisan jemaah menteri. "Individu yang cuba melobi ini menggunakan taktik yang sangat memalukan. Haus dan lapar jawatan ini bukan budaya PKR. â€œKini cuba menggunakan ketua-ketua cabang untuk kepentingan peribadi. "Tindakan seperti ini mencemarkan prinsip perjuangan parti dan harus dihentikan segera. "Saya meminta agar pucuk pimpinan agar membuat arahan larangan (melobi jawatan) supaya tidak ada membuat lobi untuk jawatan menteri," katanya. Malaysiakini telah menghubungi pemimpin berkenaan dan masih belum menerima penjelasan lanjut mengenai dakwaan ini. Dalam pada itu, dua lagi sumber PKR memberitahu memang berlaku usaha mengumpul tandatangan untuk menyokong pemimpin tersebut mendapat jawatan menteri. "Saya tak boleh dedahkan maklumat saya. Tapi, saya boleh sahkan pembantu pemimpin itu menghubungi saya untuk tandatangan surat sokongan," kata satu sumber dari Kedah. "Memang ada panggilan daripadanya. Kami belum memberi kata putus," tambah satu lagi sumber yang enggan dinamakan. Untuk rekod, Menteri Sumber Asli dan Kelestarian Alam Nik Nazmi mengemukakan surat peletakan jawatan pada 28 Mei, susulan tindakan sama oleh Menteri Ekonomi Rafizi Ramli. Kedua-duanya memetik kekalahan dalam pemilihan parti sebagai antara faktor utama pengunduran mereka. #kerajaangagalphbn #politikmalaysia

SUNGAI BULOH: Deputy Entrepreneur Development and Cooperatives Minister Datuk Seri R.   Image credit: MCOBA / Nurul Izzah FBA day after Rafizi and Nik Nazmi announced their resignation from cabinet, Tengku Zafrul announced that he has joined PKR.  Azmi Hassan of Akademi Nusantara has already poured cold water on the move by saying Tengku Zafrul move is bound to flop, in the sense that Azmi believes that Tengku Zafrul is bound to do as badly in PKR as he has done in Umno, but I beg to differ. I think Tengku Zafrul will do great in PKR. He will do so great that if I were a betting man, I bet that if Nurul Izzah becomes the next PM of the country, Tengku Zafrul might likely be her Deputy Prime Minister. The problem with Tengku Zafrul in Umno is that Umno is an identity-based party rather than a performance-based party, and Tengku Zafrul is basically hopeless in the subject of identity-based politics. To play identity politics, you have to do things like be seen drinking Teh Tarik at a warung, attending weddings and funerals in your constituency, parade around with a bag of rice in relief centres in times of flood, talk about race and religion, help your supporters by giving them things like a surat sokongan and petrol money,  and litter your speeches with quotes from the scripture.If you do things like this, your constituents will think that you are one of them, and they will then vote for you, because they will feel that if you win, it is akin to them winning too. Tengku Zafrul however, is more of a performance-based politician than he is an identity based one. His forte is in finding ways to make win-win deals with corporations or other countries, so as to increase our opportunity to win, grow, progress and become more prosperous. In Umno, it is inevitable that someone like him will be underappreciated, and perhaps even denigrated, for not â€œearningâ€ the right to become a minister, as per Umnoâ€™s value system, simply because he doesnâ€™t play the identity game that all other Umno politicians play.As a category of politician, Tengku Zafrul is probably more of a â€œtechnocratâ€, similar to Rafizi or Anthony Loke, than he is to the likes of Hadi, Muhyiddin or Anwar, who are chiefly identity based politicians. Even compared to Rafizi and Anthony Loke, Tengku Zafrul is much more of a â€œtechnocratâ€,  because even Anthony Loke and Rafizi play the identity game to an extent, but Tengku Zafrul is almost exclusively playing the performance game. A big part of the reason why Tengku Zafrul is probably the only politician who has managed to stay on as a minister from Muhyiddinâ€™s time to Ismail Sabriâ€™s time to Anwarâ€™s time, is precisely because everybody at the top needs a technocrat. You can rise to the top by playing identity politics â€“ or by making everybody believe that you are one of them and you are for them â€“ but to stay on top, you will have to provide the people with victories, growth, progress and prosperity. People like Ismail Sabri, Anwar and Muhyiddin might be able to rise to the top by making their party members or the general public believe that they are one of them and that a victory for them is equal to the victory for the public or the party, but once they are at the top, the public and the voters will only remain identified with them, if they are able to generate victories, growth, progress and prosperity.This is where people like Tengku Zafrul come in.Identity politics might be a mind game but victory, growth, progress and prosperity are matters related to reality . It doesnâ€™t matter how many people in this world believe in you, for as long as you donâ€™t create the conditions in reality that will allow you to win, grow, progress and prosper, you are not going to be able to win, grow, progress and prosper. To enable the condition for you to win, grow, progress and prosper, you actually have to focus on reality, not on changing the heart and mind of people. In other words, you have to crunch the numbers, and study how much resources, manpower, time, space, opportunity and advantage you have, and come up with a plan to optimise what you have, so that you can come up with a plan where you can win, grow, progress and prosper.  Other than the fact that Tengku Zafrul is someone that someone at the top like Anwar can count on to focus on reality, crunch the numbers and enable the condition to generate the  growth, progress and prosperity that not only the country needs, but he himself needs to stay in power,  Tengku Zafrul also has the additional benefit of being someone that will likely never challenge someone at at the top, simply because he has no interest or know how in playing the identity game in politics.The problem with Rafizi, although he was seen to be a technocrat, just like Tengku Zafrul, is that not only was he not a very successful technocrat, who could be counted to be bring such things as the PADU system to fruition, he also posed a threat to Anwar, in that he clearly has ambitions to be the number 1, as well as the ability to play the identity game that might allow him to overtake Anwar as PKRâ€™s number 1. With Rafiziâ€™s departure, Tengku Zafrul is the perfect replacement that Anwar requires, because Tengku Zafrul is likely not only a better technocrat than Rafizi, he is most likely never going to challenge Anwar, or Nurul Izzah, for the top position.I actually see the Tengku Zafrul and Nurul Izzah combo in somewhat the same light  as the  Sonia Gandhi and Manmohan Singh combo of India. Manmohan Singh was also a technocrat, who set the foundations for Indiaâ€™s transformation from a bureaucratic laden and inefficient economy that it was in the past, to become one of the economic powerhouses of modern times. Despite that, he never once did try to usurp the position of Sonia Gandhi, as the leader of the Congress party of India and the defacto leader of India at the time. Currently, our two DPMâ€™s, be it Fadhillah and Zahid Hamidi, are simply our DPMâ€™s because of a political compromise. In the next general election however, if PH is able to win in a much stronger position, and thus no longer requires to give out the DPM position to other parties, as a political compromise, it might come to pass that the DPM position will go to someone like Tengku Zafrul, who can be counted to use their position to generate results, but not use it as a platform to topple the number 1. For all you know, even if it comes to pass that for whatever reason, Nurul Izzah cannot replace Anwar as the number 1, like Manmohan Singh, Tengku Zafrul might be the best person, both for Anwarâ€™s family and the country, that stand in as the number 1. Not only will their technocratic nature help the country forward, their lack of capability to play identity based politics will be able to reassure Anwarâ€™s family that power will still be securely in their hand, even if they are not the ones in the number 1 position.
